               Portuguese Americans
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>

         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
          <ul>
           <li class="nv-view">
            <a href="/wiki/Template:Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Template:Hispanic and Latino Americans">
             <abbr title="View this template">
              v
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-talk">
            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Template talk:Hispanic and Latino Americans">
             <abbr title="Discuss this template">
              t
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-edit">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans&amp;action=edit">

              e
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>

       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       is the second most spoken
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_United_States" title="Languages of the United States">
        language in the United States of America
       </a>
       . Forty-five million
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Hispanophones
       </a>
       speak Spanish as their
       <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">
        first
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">
        second
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Heritage_language" title="Heritage language">
        heritage language
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and there are six million Spanish language students in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This makes the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       the third-largest
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">
        Hispanophone
       </a>
       country in the world after
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       , and before
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       . Spanish has both the largest number of native language
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance speakers
       </a>
       and native
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European language speakers
       </a>
       in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Más_'speak_spanish'_que_en_España_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Más_'speak_spanish'_que_en_España-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       About half of all American Spanish speakers also assessed themselves as speaking English "very well" in the 2000
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census" title="U.S. Census">
        U.S. Census
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2000_Census,_Language_in_the_US_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2000_Census,_Language_in_the_US-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There are more Spanish-speakers in the United States than speakers of
       <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_the_United_States" title="French language in the United States">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/German_language_in_the_United_States" title="German language in the United States">
        German
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language_in_the_United_States" title="Italian language in the United States">
        Italian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_language" title="Hawaiian language">
        Hawaiian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_language_in_the_United_States" title="Chinese language in the United States">
        varieties of Chinese
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_languages" title="Native American languages">
        Native American languages
       </a>
       combined. According to the 2012 American Community Survey conducted by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">
        U.S. Census Bureau
       </a>
       , Spanish is the primary language spoken at home by 38.3 million people aged five or older, more than twice that of 1990.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012_survey_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2012_survey-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Spanish language has been present in what is now the United States since the 16th and 17th centuries, with the arrival of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        Spanish colonization
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
        North America
       </a>
       . Colonizers settled in areas that would later become the states of
       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
        Florida
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">
        Colorado
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">
        New Mexico
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">
        Arizona
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">
        Nevada
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">
        Utah
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">
        Spanish explorers
       </a>
       explored areas of 42 future
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
        U.S. states
       </a>
       leaving behind a varying range of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">
        Hispanic
       </a>
       legacy in the North American continent. Western regions of the
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Territory" title="Louisiana Territory">
        Louisiana Territory
       </a>
       were also under Spanish rule between 1763 and 1800, after the
       <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">
        French and Indian War
       </a>
       , further extending the Spanish influence throughout the modern-day United States of America.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the incorporation of these areas into the United States in the first half of the 19th century, the Spanish language was later reinforced in the country by the acquisition of
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       in 1898. Later waves of emigration from
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
        El Salvador
       </a>
       and elsewhere in
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">
        Hispanic America
       </a>
       to the United States beginning in the second half of the 19th century to the present-day have strengthened the role of the Spanish language in the country. Today,
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Hispanics
       </a>
       are one of the fastest growing ethnic groups in the United States, thus increasing the use and importance of American Spanish in the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RUIDIAZ(1893)_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1325" data-file-width="1019" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg/200px-RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg/300px-RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg/400px-RUIDIAZ%281893%29_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RUIDIAZ(1893)_1.083_JUAN_PONCE_DE_LE%C3%93N.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">
          Juan Ponce de León
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Santerv%C3%A1s_de_Campos" title="Santervás de Campos">
          Santervás de Campos
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Valladolid" title="Province of Valladolid">
          Valladolid
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
          Spain
         </a>
         ). He was one of the first Europeans to arrive to the current United States because he led the first European expedition to
         <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">
          Florida
         </a>
         , which he named. Spanish was the first European language spoken in the territory that is now the United States.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="History of Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        History of Hispanic and Latino Americans
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Spanish_settlements">
        Early Spanish settlements
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early Spanish settlements">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Spanish was among the very first European
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_North_America" title="Languages of North America">
        languages spoken in North America
       </a>
       , preceded only by
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">
        Old Norse
       </a>
       . Spanish arrived in the territory of the modern United States with
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">
        Ponce de León
       </a>
       in 1513. In 1565, the
       <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">
        Spaniards
       </a>
       founded
       <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">
        St. Augustine, Florida
       </a>
       , and as of the early 1800s, it became the oldest continuously occupied European settlement in what is now the United States. In 1898, San Juan, the capital of Puerto Rico, became the oldest city in all of the U.S. territory: Juan Ponce De León founded San Juan in 1508.
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically, the Spanish-speaking population increased because of territorial annexation of lands claimed earlier by the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       and by wars with Mexico and by land purchases, while
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        modern factors
       </a>
       continue increasing the size of this population.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1819 Florida was sold by
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       to the United States by
       <a href="/wiki/Adams%E2%80%93On%C3%ADs_Treaty" title="Adams–Onís Treaty">
        Adams–Onís Treaty
       </a>
       ; many Spanish settlers, whose ancestors came from Cuba, Andalusia, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
        Canary Islands
       </a>
       , became U.S. citizens and continued to speak Spanish.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Louisiana_Purchase_.281803.E2.80.931804.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana_Purchase_(1803–1804)">
        Louisiana Purchase (1803–1804)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Louisiana Purchase (1803–1804)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">
        Louisiana Purchase
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the late 18th and early 19th centuries, land claimed by Spain encompassed a large part of the contemporary U.S. territory, including the French colony of Louisiana that was under Spanish occupation from 1769 to 1800, and then part of the United States since 1803. When
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_Spain)" title="Louisiana (New Spain)">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       was
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">
        sold to the United States
       </a>
       , its Spanish and
       <a href="/wiki/Cajun_French" title="Cajun French">
        Cajun French
       </a>
       inhabitants became U.S. citizens, and continued to speak Spanish or French. In 1813,
       <a href="/wiki/George_Ticknor" title="George Ticknor">
        George Ticknor
       </a>
       started a program of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Studies" title="Spanish Studies">
        Spanish Studies
       </a>
       at Harvard University.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garcia_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Garcia-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Annexation_of_Texas_and_the_Mexican.E2.80.93American_War">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Annexation_of_Texas_and_the_Mexican–American_War">
        Annexation of Texas and the Mexican–American War
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Annexation of Texas and the Mexican–American War">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg/220px-St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg/330px-St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg/440px-St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St_Aug_Lindsley_House_sign01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Spanish language heritage in Florida dates back to 1565, with the founding of
         <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">
          Saint Augustine, Florida
         </a>
         . Spanish was the first European language spoken in Florida.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1821,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">
        Mexico's War of Independence
       </a>
       from Spain, Texas was part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Mexican_States" title="United Mexican States">
        United Mexican States
       </a>
       as the state of
       <a href="/wiki/Coahuila_y_Tejas" title="Coahuila y Tejas">
        Coahuila y Tejas
       </a>
       . A large influx of Americans soon followed, originally with the approval of Mexico's president. In 1836, the now largely "American" Texans fought a war of independence from the central government of Mexico and established the Republic of Texas. In 1846, the Republic dissolved when Texas entered the United States of America as a state. Per the 1850 U.S. census, fewer than 16,000 Texans were of Mexican descent, and nearly all were Spanish-speaking people (both Mexicans and non-Spanish European settlers who include
       <a href="/wiki/German_Texan" title="German Texan">
        German Texan
       </a>
       ) who were outnumbered (six-to-one) by English-speaking settlers (both Americans and other immigrant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" title="European ethnic groups">
        Europeans
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">
        Mexican War of Independence
       </a>
       from Spain,
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">
        Nevada
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">
        Arizona
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">
        Utah
       </a>
       , western
       <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">
        Colorado
       </a>
       and southwestern
       <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">
        Wyoming
       </a>
       also became part of the Mexican territory of
       <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">
        Alta California
       </a>
       . Most of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">
        New Mexico
       </a>
       , western Texas, southern
       <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">
        Colorado
       </a>
       , southwestern
       <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">
        Kansas
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">
        Oklahoma
       </a>
       panhandle were part of the territory of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">
        Santa Fe de Nuevo México
       </a>
       . The geographical isolation and unique political history of this territory led to
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_Spanish" title="New Mexican Spanish">
        New Mexican Spanish
       </a>
       differing notably from both Spanish spoken in other parts of the United States of America and Spanish spoken in the present-day United Mexican States.
      </p>
      <p>
       Mexico lost almost half of the northern territory gained from Spain in 1821 to the United States in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">
        Mexican–American War
       </a>
       (1846–1848). This included parts of contemporary Texas, and Colorado, Arizona, New Mexico, Wyoming, California, Nevada, and Utah. Although the lost territory was sparsely populated, the thousands of Spanish-speaking Mexicans subsequently became U.S. citizens. The war-ending
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">
        Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo
       </a>
       (1848) does not explicitly address language. However, the English-speaking American settlers who entered the Southwest established their language, culture, and law as dominant, to the extent it fully displaced Spanish in the
       <a href="/wiki/Public_sphere" title="Public sphere">
        public sphere
       </a>
       . In 1855, California declared that English would be the only
       <a href="/wiki/Medium_of_instruction" title="Medium of instruction">
        medium of instruction
       </a>
       in its schools; the newly admitted state of
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">
        New Mexico
       </a>
       followed suit in 1891 to mandate that all of its schools teach in English only.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garcia_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Garcia-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first California constitutional convention in 1849 had eight
       <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">
        Californio
       </a>
       participants; the resulting state constitution was produced in English and Spanish, and it contained a clause requiring all published laws and regulations to be published in both languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Valdés_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Valdés-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the very first acts of the first
       <a href="/wiki/California_State_Legislature" title="California State Legislature">
        California Legislature
       </a>
       of 1850 was to authorize the appointment of a State Translator, who would be responsible for translating all state laws, decrees, documents, or orders into Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Martin-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       But the state's second constitutional convention in 1872 had
       <i>
        no
       </i>
       Spanish-speaking participants; the convention's English-speaking participants felt that the state's remaining minority of Spanish-speakers should simply learn English; and the convention ultimately voted 46-39 to revise the earlier clause so that all official proceedings would henceforth be published only in English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Valdés_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Valdés-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Spanish.E2.80.93American_War_.281898.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish–American_War_(1898)">
        Spanish–American War (1898)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spanish–American War (1898)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1898, consequent to the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">
        Spanish–American War
       </a>
       , the United States took control of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">
        Philippines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">
        Guam
       </a>
       as American territories. In 1902, Cuba became independent from the United States, while Puerto Rico remained a U.S. territory. The American government required government services to be bilingual in Spanish and English, and attempted to introduce English-medium education to Puerto Rico, but the latter effort was unsuccessful.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LP_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LP-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1917, the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Association_of_Teachers_of_Spanish_and_Portuguese" title="American Association of Teachers of Spanish and Portuguese">
        American Association of Teachers of Spanish and Portuguese
       </a>
       was founded, and the academic study of Spanish literature was helped by negative attitudes towards
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       due to World War I. From 1942 to 1962, the
       <a href="/wiki/Bracero_program" title="Bracero program">
        Bracero program
       </a>
       would provide for mass Mexican migration to the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garcia_7-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Garcia-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Once Puerto Rico was granted autonomy in 1948, even mainlander officials who came to Puerto Rico were forced to learn Spanish. Only 20% of Puerto Rico's residents understand English, and although the island's government had a policy of official bilingualism, it was repealed in favor of a Spanish-only policy in 1991. This policy was reversed in 1993 when a
       <a href="/wiki/Statehood_movement_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Statehood movement in Puerto Rico">
        pro-statehood
       </a>
       party ousted a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_independence" title="Puerto Rican independence">
        pro-independence
       </a>
       party from the commonwealth government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LP_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-LP-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_mass_migration">
        Modern mass migration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern mass migration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The relatively recent but large influx of Spanish-speakers to the United States has increased the overall total of Spanish-speakers in the country. They form majorities and large minorities in many political districts, especially in California, Arizona, New Mexico, and Texas, the American states bordering Mexico, and also in
       <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">
        South Florida
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Mexicans first moved to the United States as refugees in the turmoil of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">
        Mexican Revolution
       </a>
       from 1910–1917, but many more emigrated later for economic reasons. The large majority of Mexicans are in the former Mexican-controlled areas in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">
        Southwest
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       At over 5 million, Puerto Ricans are easily the second largest Hispanic group. Of all major Hispanic groups, Puerto Ricans are the least likely to be proficient in Spanish, but millions of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Americans" title="Puerto Rican Americans">
        Puerto Rican Americans
       </a>
       living in the U.S. mainland nonetheless are fluent in Spanish. Puerto Ricans are natural-born U.S. citizens, and many Puerto Ricans have migrated to
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orlando" title="Orlando">
        Orlando
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">
        Philadelphia
       </a>
       , and other areas of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_United_States" title="Eastern United States">
        Eastern United States
       </a>
       , increasing the Spanish-speaking populations and in some areas being the majority of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">
        Hispanophone
       </a>
       population, especially in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Florida" title="Central Florida">
        Central Florida
       </a>
       . In Hawaii, where Puerto Rican farm laborers and Mexican ranchers have settled since the late 19th century, seven percent of the islands' people are either Hispanic or Hispanophone or both.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">
        Cuban Revolution
       </a>
       of 1959 created a community of
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_exile" title="Cuban exile">
        Cuban exiles
       </a>
       who opposed the Communist revolution, many of whom left for the United States. In 1963, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ford_Foundation" title="Ford Foundation">
        Ford Foundation
       </a>
       established the first bilingual education program in the United States for the children of Cuban exiles in
       <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">
        Miami-Dade County, Florida
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Nationality_Act_of_1965" title="Immigration and Nationality Act of 1965">
        Immigration and Nationality Act of 1965
       </a>
       boosted immigration from Latin American countries, and in 1968, Congress passed the
       <a href="/wiki/Bilingual_Education_Act" title="Bilingual Education Act">
        Bilingual Education Act
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garcia_7-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Garcia-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of these one million
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Americans" title="Cuban Americans">
        Cuban Americans
       </a>
       settled in southern and central Florida, while other
       <a href="/wiki/Cubans" title="Cubans">
        Cubans
       </a>
       live in the Northeastern United States; most are fluent in Spanish. In the city of Miami today Spanish is the first language mostly due to Cuban immigration. Likewise, the
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_Revolution" title="Nicaraguan Revolution">
        Nicaraguan Revolution
       </a>
       promoted a migration of
       <a href="/wiki/Contras" title="Contras">
        Contras
       </a>
       who were opposed to the socialist government in Nicaragua, to the United States in the late 1980s.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Most of these
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguans" title="Nicaraguans">
        Nicaraguans
       </a>
       migrated to Florida, California and Texas.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg/250px-SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg/375px-SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg/500px-SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/SER-Ni%C3%B1os_Charter_School" title="SER-Niños Charter School">
          SER-Niños Charter School
         </a>
         , a K–8 bilingual public school in
         <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">
          Houston
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
          Texas
         </a>
         .
         <a href="/wiki/Bilingual_education" title="Bilingual education">
          Bilingual education
         </a>
         is popular in school districts with large numbers of Spanish-speakers.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The exodus of
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadorans" title="Salvadorans">
        Salvadorans
       </a>
       was a result of both economic and political problems. The largest immigration wave occurred as a result of the
       <a href="/wiki/Salvadoran_Civil_War" title="Salvadoran Civil War">
        Salvadoran Civil War
       </a>
       in the 1980s, in which 20 to 30 percent of
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
        El Salvador
       </a>
       's population emigrated. About 50 percent, or up to 500,000 of those who escaped, headed to the United States, which was already home to over 10,000 Salvadorans, making Salvadoran Americans the fourth-largest Hispanic and Latino American group, after the Mexican-American majority, stateside Puerto Ricans, and Cubans.
      </p>
      <p>
       As civil wars engulfed several Central American countries in the 1980s, hundreds of thousands of Salvadorans fled their country and came to the United States. Between 1980 and 1990, the Salvadoran immigrant population in the United States increased nearly fivefold from 94,000 to 465,000. The number of Salvadoran immigrants in the United States continued to grow in the 1990s and 2000s as a result of family reunification and new arrivals fleeing a series of natural disasters that hit El Salvador, including earthquakes and hurricanes. By 2008, there were about 1.1 million Salvadoran immigrants in the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
       Until the 20th century, there was no clear record of the number of Venezuelans who emigrated to the United States. Between the 18th and early 19th centuries, there were many European immigrants who went to
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuela
       </a>
       , only to later migrate to the United States along with their children and grandchildren who were born and/or grew up in Venezuela speaking Spanish. From 1910 to 1930, it is estimated that over 4,000 South Americans each year emigrated to the United States; however, there are few specific figures indicating these statistics. Many
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuelans" title="Venezuelans">
        Venezuelans
       </a>
       settled in the United States with hopes of receiving a better education, only to remain there following graduation. They are frequently joined by relatives. However, since the early 1980s, the reasons for Venezuelan emigration have changed to include hopes of earning a higher salary and due to the economic fluctuations in Venezuela which also promoted an important migration of Venezuelan professionals to the US.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everyculture:Venezuelan_American_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Everyculture:Venezuelan_American-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 2000s, dissident
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuelans" title="Venezuelans">
        Venezuelans
       </a>
       migrated to
       <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">
        South Florida
       </a>
       , especially the
       <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">
        suburbs
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Doral,_Florida" title="Doral, Florida">
        Doral
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Weston,_Florida" title="Weston, Florida">
        Weston
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Other main states with Venezuelan American populations are, according to the 1990 census,
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">
        New York
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       (adding to their existing Hispanic populations),
       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
        New Jersey
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">
        Massachusetts
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">
        Maryland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everyculture:Venezuelan_American_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Everyculture:Venezuelan_American-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Refugees from Spain also migrated to the U.S. due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">
        Spanish Civil War
       </a>
       (1936 - 1939) and political instability
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spain_under_Franco" title="Spain under Franco">
        under the regime of Francisco Franco
       </a>
       that lasted until 1975. The majority of Spaniards settled in Florida, Texas, California,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">
        New Jersey
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The publication of data by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">
        United States Census Bureau
       </a>
       in 2003 revealed that Hispanics were the largest minority in the United States and caused a flurry of press speculation in Spain about the position of Spanish in the United States.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       That year, the
       <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cervantes" title="Instituto Cervantes">
        Instituto Cervantes
       </a>
       , an organization created by the Spanish government in 1991 to promote Spanish language around the globe, established a branch in New York.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">
        Geographic distribution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_United_States" title="Languages of the United States">
        Languages of the United States
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._cities_by_Spanish-speaking_population" title="List of U.S. cities by Spanish-speaking population">
        List of U.S. cities by Spanish-speaking population
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="float:right; margin-left:1em; font-size:88%">

      <p>
       In total, there were 36,995,602 people aged five or older in the United States who spoke Spanish at home (12.8% of the total U.S. population).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010_survey_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010_survey-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_status">
        Current status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Current status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg/220px-Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg/330px-Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg/440px-Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Berclair_Elementary_School_sign_in_Spanish_Memphis_TN_2013-01-01_015.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Public elementary school sign in Spanish in
         <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">
          Memphis, Tennessee
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USCISLogoSpanish.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="375" height="59" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/USCISLogoSpanish.jpg/220px-USCISLogoSpanish.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/USCISLogoSpanish.jpg/330px-USCISLogoSpanish.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5f/USCISLogoSpanish.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USCISLogoSpanish.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Spanish-language logo of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Citizenship_and_Immigration_Services" title="U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services">
          U.S. Citizenship and Immigration Services
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although the United States has no de jure
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       , English is the dominant language of business, education, government, religion, media, culture,
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">
        civil society
       </a>
       , and the public sphere. Virtually all state and federal government agencies and large corporations use English as their internal
       <a href="/wiki/Working_language" title="Working language">
        working language
       </a>
       , especially at the management level. Some states, such as
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">
        New Mexico
       </a>
       , provide bilingual legislated notices and official documents, in Spanish and English, and other commonly used languages. English is the home language of most Americans, including a growing proportion of Hispanic Americans; between 2000 and 2015, the proportion of Hispanics who spoke Spanish at home decreased from 78 to 73 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ajspanish_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ajspanish-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As noted above, the only major exception is the U.S. Commonwealth of Puerto Rico, where Spanish is the official and most commonly used language.
      </p>
      <p>
       Throughout the history of the Southwest United States, the controversial issue of language as part of cultural rights and bilingual state government representation has caused socio-cultural friction between Anglophones and Hispanophones. Currently, Spanish is the most widely taught
       <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">
        second language
       </a>
       in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="California">
        California
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: California">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       California's first constitution recognized Spanish language rights:
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        All laws, decrees, regulations, and provisions emanating from any of the three supreme powers of this State, which from their nature require publication, shall be published in English and Spanish.
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_Constitution" title="California Constitution">
          California Constitution
         </a>
         , 1849, Art. 11 Sec. 21.
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       By 1870, English-speaking Americans were a majority in California; in 1879, the state promulgated a new constitution under which all official proceedings were to be conducted exclusively in English, a clause that remained in effect until 1966. In 1986, California voters added a new constitutional clause, by
       <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">
        referendum
       </a>
       , stating that:
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        English is the official language of the State of California.
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         California Constitution, Art. 3, Sec. 6
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       Spanish remains widely spoken throughout the state, and many government forms, documents, and services are bilingual, in English and Spanish. And although all official proceedings are to be conducted in English:
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        A person unable to understand English who is charged with a crime has a right to an interpreter throughout the proceedings.
       </p>
       <div class="templatequotecite">
        —
        <cite>
         California Constitution, Art. 1. Sec. 14
        </cite>
       </div>
      </blockquote>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arizona">
        Arizona
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Arizona">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The state (like its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Southwest" title="American Southwest">
        southwestern
       </a>
       neighbors) has had close linguistic and cultural ties with Mexico. The state outside the
       <a href="/wiki/Gadsden_Purchase" title="Gadsden Purchase">
        Gadsden Purchase
       </a>
       of 1853 was part of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Territory" title="New Mexico Territory">
        New Mexico Territory
       </a>
       until 1863, when the western half was made into the
       <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Territory" title="Arizona Territory">
        Arizona Territory
       </a>
       . The area of the former Gadsden Purchase contained a majority of Spanish-speakers until the 1940s, although the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tucson" title="Tucson">
        Tucson
       </a>
       area had a higher ratio of anglophones (including Mexican Americans who were fluent in English); the continuous arrival of Mexican settlers increases the number of Spanish-speakers.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_Mexico">
        New Mexico
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: New Mexico">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_Spanish" title="New Mexican Spanish">
        New Mexican Spanish
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       New Mexico is commonly thought to have Spanish as an official language alongside English because of its wide usage and legal promotion of Spanish in the state; however, the state has no official language. New Mexico's laws are promulgated bilingually in Spanish and English. Although English is the state government's paper working language, government business is often conducted in Spanish, particularly at the local level. Spanish has been spoken in the New Mexico-Colorado border and the contemporary
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S.%E2%80%93Mexico_border" title="U.S.–Mexico border">
        U.S.–Mexico border
       </a>
       since the 16th century.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of its relative isolation from other Spanish-speaking areas over most of its 400-year existence, New Mexico Spanish, and in particular the Spanish of northern New Mexico and Colorado has retained many elements of 16th- and 17th-century Spanish and has developed its own vocabulary.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cobos-1_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cobos-1-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, it contains many words from
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       , the language currently spoken by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahua_people" title="Nahua people">
        Nahua people
       </a>
       in Mexico. New Mexican Spanish also contains loan words from the
       <a href="/wiki/Pueblo" title="Pueblo">
        Pueblo
       </a>
       languages of the upper
       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">
        Rio Grande Valley
       </a>
       , Mexican-Spanish words (
       <i>
        mexicanismos
       </i>
       ), and borrowings from English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cobos-1_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cobos-1-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Grammatical changes include the loss of the second person verb form, changes in verb endings, particularly in the
       <a href="/wiki/Preterite" title="Preterite">
        preterite
       </a>
       , and partial merging of the second and third conjugations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cobos-2_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cobos-2-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Texas">
        Texas
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Texas">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG/220px-NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG/330px-NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG/440px-NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NoSmokingTexasDeptStateHealth.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         "No Smoking" sign in Spanish and English at the headquarters of the
         <a href="/wiki/Texas_Department_of_State_Health_Services" title="Texas Department of State Health Services">
          Texas Department of Health
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">
          Austin, Texas
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (June 2010)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In Texas, English is the state's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">
         de facto
        </a>
       </i>
       official language (though it lacks
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">
         de jure
        </a>
       </i>
       status) and is used in government. However, the continual influx of Spanish-speaking immigrants increased the import of Spanish in Texas. Although it is a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">
        Southern United States
       </a>
       , Texas's counties bordering Mexico are mostly Hispanic, and consequently, Spanish is commonly spoken in the region. The
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Texas" title="Government of Texas">
        Government of Texas
       </a>
       , through Section 2054.116 of the Government Code, mandates that
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_agency" title="State agency">
        state agencies
       </a>
       provide information on their websites in Spanish to assist residents who have limited English proficiency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico">
        Puerto Rico
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Spanish" title="Puerto Rican Spanish">
        Puerto Rican Spanish
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Commonwealth of Puerto Rico recognizes Spanish and English as official languages; Spanish is the dominant first language.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_place_names">
        Spanish place names
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Spanish place names">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._place_names_of_Spanish_origin" title="List of U.S. place names of Spanish origin">
        List of U.S. place names of Spanish origin
       </a>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Learning_trends_in_the_United_States">
        Learning trends in the United States
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Learning trends in the United States">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Spanish is currently the most widely taught non-English language in American secondary schools and higher education.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       More than 790,000 university students were enrolled in Spanish courses in the autumn of 2013, with Spanish the most widely taught language in American colleges and universities. Some 50.6 percent of the total number of U.S. students enrolled in foreign-language courses take Spanish, followed by French (12.7%),
       <a href="/wiki/American_Sign_Language" title="American Sign Language">
        American Sign Language
       </a>
       (7%), German (5.5%), Italian (4.6%), Japanese (4.3%), and Chinese (3.9%), although the totals remain relatively small in relation to the total U.S. population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Variation">
        Variation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Variation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg/220px-WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg/330px-WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg/440px-WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WalgreenDrugStoreMiami.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         La Época is an upscale
         <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">
          Miami
         </a>
         department store, whose Spanish name comes from
         <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
          Cuba
         </a>
         . La Época is an example of the many businesses started and owned by Spanish-speakers in the United States.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The influence of English on American Spanish is very important. In many Latino
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (also called Hispanic) youth
       <a href="/wiki/Subculture" title="Subculture">
        subcultures
       </a>
       , it is fashionable to variously mix Spanish and English, thereby producing
       <a href="/wiki/Spanglish" title="Spanglish">
        Spanglish
       </a>
       .
       <i>
        Spanglish
       </i>
       is the name for the admixture of English words and phrases to Spanish for effective communication.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia_Norteamericana_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Academia Norteamericana de la Lengua Española">
         Academia Norteamericana de la Lengua Española
        </a>
       </i>
       (North American Academy of the Spanish Language) tracks the developments of the Spanish spoken in the United States, and the influences of English upon it.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_sub-types">
        Spanish sub-types
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Spanish sub-types">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Language experts distinguish the following varieties of the Spanish spoken in the United States:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Spanish" title="Mexican Spanish">
         Mexican
        </a>
        : the U.S.–Mexico border, throughout the US southwest from California to Texas, as well as the city of Chicago, but becoming ubiquitous throughout the continental United States as Mexican Spanish is used as the
        <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">
         standardized dialect
        </a>
        of Spanish in the continental United States.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Spanish" title="Caribbean Spanish">
         Caribbean Spanish
        </a>
        : Spanish as spoken by Puerto Ricans, Cubans, and Dominicans. Largely heard throughout the Northeastern United States and Florida, especially New York City and Miami, among other cities in the Eastern US.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Central_American_Spanish" title="Central American Spanish">
         Central American Spanish
        </a>
        : Spanish as spoken by Hispanics with origins in Central American countries such as El Salvador, Guatemala, Honduras, Nicaragua, Costa Rica, and Panama. Largely heard in major cities throughout California and Texas, as well as Washington DC, New York, and Miami.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_American_Spanish" title="South American Spanish">
         South American Spanish
        </a>
        : Spanish as spoken by Hispanics with origins in South American countries such as Venzuela, Colombia, Peru, and Chile. Largely heard in major cities throughout
        <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">
         New York
        </a>
        , California, Texas, and Florida.
       </li>
       <li>
        Colonial Spanish: Spanish as spoken by descendants of Spanish colonists and early Mexicans before United States expansion and annexion of the US southwest and other areas.
        <ul>
         <li>
          Californian (1769–present): California, especially the
          <a href="/wiki/Central_Coast_(California)" title="Central Coast (California)">
           Central Coast
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isle%C3%B1o_Spanish" title="Isleño Spanish">
           Isleño
          </a>
          (Islander) (18th century–present):
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Bernard_Parish" title="St. Bernard Parish">
           St. Bernard Parish
          </a>
          , Louisiana
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_Spanish" title="New Mexican Spanish">
           New Mexican Spanish
          </a>
          : Central and north-central New Mexico and south-central Colorado and the border regions of Arizona, Texas, and New Mexico, and southeastern Colorado
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Most post-first generations of Spanish-speakers tend to speak the language with American English accents of the region they grew up in.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Common_English_words_derived_from_Spanish">
        Common English words derived from Spanish
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language_in_the_United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Common English words derived from Spanish">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_words_of_Spanish_origin" title="List of English words of Spanish origin">
        List of English words of Spanish origin
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Analogously, many Spanish words are now standard American English.
      </p>
      <div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
       <ul>
        <li>
         Admiral
        </li>
        <li>
         Avocado (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           aguacate
          </span>
         </i>
         from
         <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">
          Nahuatl
         </a>
         <i>
          <span lang="nah" xml:lang="nah">
           aguacatl
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Aficionado
        </li>
        <li>
         Banana (originally from
         <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">
          Wolof
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Buckaroo (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           vaquero
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Cafeteria (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           cafetería
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Chocolate (from Nahuatl
         <i>
          <span lang="nah" xml:lang="nah">
           xocolatl
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Cigar (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           cigarro
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Corral
        </li>
        <li>
         Coyote (from Nahuatl
         <i>
          <span lang="nah" xml:lang="nah">
           coyotl
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Desperado (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           desesperado
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Guerrilla
        </li>
        <li>
         Guitar (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           guitarra
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Hurricane (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           huracán
          </span>
         </i>
         from the
         <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">
          Taíno
         </a>
         storm god
         <a href="/wiki/Jurac%C3%A1n" title="Juracán">
          Juracán
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Junta
        </li>
        <li>
         Lasso (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           lazo
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Potato (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           patata
          </span>
         </i>
         ; see
         <a href="/wiki/Potato#Etymology" title="Potato">
          Etymology of "potato"
         </a>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Ranch (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           rancho
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Rodeo
        </li>
        <li>
         Siesta
        </li>
        <li>
         Tomato (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           tomate
          </span>
         </i>
         from Nahuatl
         <i>
          <span lang="nah" xml:lang="nah">
           tomatl
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
        <li>
         Tornado
        </li>
        <li>
         Vanilla (
         <i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           vainilla
          </span>
         </i>
         )
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Logo_Univision_2013.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="410" data-file-width="508" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Logo_Univision_2013.svg/140px-Logo_Univision_2013.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Logo_Univision_2013.svg/210px-Logo_Univision_2013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Logo_Univision_2013.svg/280px-Logo_Univision_2013.svg.png 2x" width="140"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Logo_Univision_2013.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Univisi%C3%B3n" title="Univisión">
          Univisión
         </a>
         is the country's largest Spanish language network, followed by
         <a href="/wiki/Telemundo" title="Telemundo">
          Telemundo
         </a>
         . It is the country's fourth-largest network overall.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
          <a href="#cite_note-28">
           [28]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
